  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_3126cd99-a8e9-469f-b2f6-9fe2ca0cd2dc'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText12279920714265989038" style="display:none">Before Peter Pan belonged to Wendy, he belonged to the girl with the crow feather in her hair...<br /><br />Fifteen-year-old Tiger Lily doesn't believe in love stories or happy endings. Then she meets the alluring teenage Peter Pan in the forbidden woods of Neverland and immediately falls under his spell.<br /><br />Peter is unlike anyone she's ever known. Impetuous and brave, he both scares and enthralls her. As the leader of the Lost Boys, the most fearsome of Neverland's inhabitants, Peter is an unthinkable match for Tiger Lily. Soon, she is risking everything—her family, her future—to be with him. When she is faced with marriage to a terrible man in her own tribe, she must choose between the life she's always known and running away to an uncertain future with Peter.<br /><br />With enemies threatening to tear them apart, the lovers seem doomed. But it's the arrival of Wendy Darling, an English girl who's everything Tiger Lily is not, that leads Tiger Lily to discover that the most dangerous enemies can live inside even the most loyal and loving heart.<br /><br />From the New York Times bestselling author of Peaches comes a magical and bewitching story of the romance between a fearless heroine and the boy who wouldn't grow up.</span>

<div id="review_292421743" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/292421743" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/292421743?book_show_action=true">Mar 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062003256" href="/book/show/12924326-tiger-lily">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Emily May by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/283407-crowinator">Crowinator</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=coverly-love">coverly-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer292421743" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6313883875594376484">Edit 04/04/2013: I read this almost a year ago now and it still haunts me in the best possible way. So I just wanted to share <a href='http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=7GSyXcqvFXA' rel='nofollow noopener'>this song</a> with you because it reminds me of this book so much.<br/><br/>.............................................................................<br/><br/><br/><b>
  <i>"Sometimes I think that maybe we are just stories. Like we may as well just be words on a page, because we're only what we've done and what we are going to do."</i>
</b><br/><br/>Everything about the appearance and description of this book it seems i</span>
  <span id="freeText6313883875594376484" style="display:none">Edit 04/04/2013: I read this almost a year ago now and it still haunts me in the best possible way. So I just wanted to share <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=7GSyXcqvFXA" rel="nofollow noopener">this song</a> with you because it reminds me of this book so much.<br /><br />.............................................................................<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <i>"Sometimes I think that maybe we are just stories. Like we may as well just be words on a page, because we're only what we've done and what we are going to do."</i>
</b><br /><br />Everything about the appearance and description of this book it seems is geared towards the wrong audience. If it hadn't been for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/285029707" rel="nofollow noopener">Crowinator's review</a> I would have written this off as another cheesy romance that's okay when you're eight years old and watching a disney film but should otherwise be avoided. There are a number of readers I can see picking this up: romance enthusiasts, those who enjoy novels that are like disney films, or those who've read Anderson's other books (girl scouts and teen troubles). They will probably be disappointed.<br /><br />How best can I put this? I know, I'll use TV shows! Let's take 90210 first of all. This is a show about rich people, celebrities, first world problems and a lifestyle with glitter on it. It's about life in Los Angeles. You know what else is about life in LA? Angel (Buffy spin-off). But Angel tells a different story, one of dingy backstreets, prostitutes, drug addicts and criminals. It's the same city but it's the story of lives that don't sparkle. If you're wondering how this is at all relevant, well, Peter Pan is 90210, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7514925.Tiger_Lily" title="Tiger Lily by Jodi Lynn Anderson" rel="nofollow noopener">Tiger Lily</a> is Angel.<br /><br />This novel tells the tale of the dark underbelly of Neverland where the good guys don't always win and love doesn't always triumph. It's so much darker and sadder than I could have possibly imagined. Even though we are told from the start that this is a love story, it is more than that. It's about loss and loneliness and fear of change. Because who would fear change more than those who'd never had to experience growing up and dying? <br /><br />Tiger Lily is one of the loneliest characters ever. Her other tribe members believe her to be cursed and she has long battled against the torment of not quite being accepted. After one misstep too many, she is told she must marry Giant - a violent oaf of a man who mistreats her whenever the chance presents itself. It is only natural that when she discovers a boy out in the forest who's almost as lonely as she is that she would fall in love with him. <br /><br />By telling the story from Tinkerbell's point of view, we are able to hear it on a very personal level and get a close look at all the characters individually whilst having a wider scope than normal 1st person allows. The story itself is cleverly woven with elements of the one we know from disney and the original book. Did you ever wonder how a crocodile came to be hanging around with a ticking clock down his throat? Well, now I know. <br /><br />The villains in this story are as complex as everyone else and Anderson offers new and interesting traits for familiar characters. James Hook is a sad, old man who came to Neverland on dreams of staying young forever - but his mission failed. He has since then lost himself to drink and his obsession with Peter Pan; Hook's hatred for himself and the world around him is all channelled into his hatred for Peter. Also, Smee (remember him?) is a strange case who murders those he admires for their strength and beauty but then mourns their deaths.<br /><br />The "Englanders" in this book share obvious parallels with the settlers in North America. Tiger Lily's tribe rescue an injured Englander and nurse him back to full health, but once he is back on his feet he begins "educating" the tribe in the rules of God and what is appropriate dress and how those who don't fulfill their purpose will not go to heaven. You can see how easily it would be to change people through fear of eternal punishment; how to easily put what-ifs in their minds and make them question what they've always believed. <br /><br />So, this is not the story I expected to read. But it's beautiful. I loved the writing style and the characters. The people in this book have their strengths and they have their weaknesses, and sometimes those weaknesses are too much for them to handle. The ending is both happy and sad. It isn't the one you wanted but I guess that's life for you.<br /><br /><a href="http://emilymay.me" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6313883875594376484" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer18409355165804029191">bumping this up to 5 stars because im honestly feeling downright obsessed with this story. ive always romanticised the idea of peter pan and his lost boys, so i knew i would enjoy this, but wow. i was not expecting such a soft and beautiful story.<br/><br/>the gorgeous prose is definitely what creates such an emotionally compelling narrative. i felt each word slowly makes its way into my heart and plant itself there, growing larger with each page. i loved tinkerbell as a narrator and i grew fond of her as</span>
  <span id="freeText18409355165804029191" style="display:none">bumping this up to 5 stars because im honestly feeling downright obsessed with this story. ive always romanticised the idea of peter pan and his lost boys, so i knew i would enjoy this, but wow. i was not expecting such a soft and beautiful story.<br /><br />the gorgeous prose is definitely what creates such an emotionally compelling narrative. i felt each word slowly makes its way into my heart and plant itself there, growing larger with each page. i loved tinkerbell as a narrator and i grew fond of her as a character because of it. i enjoy how she had such an omnipresent view of neverland and really appreciated the story she told of tiger lily and peter. <br /><br />this book is definitely an unexpected, but very welcome, surprise - in more ways than one. <br /><br /><b>↠ <i>4.5 stars</i></b></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1722255942" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1722255942" />
    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1722255942?book_show_action=true">Aug 08, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=2017-reads">2017-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=retellings">retellings</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1722255942" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9270968925727650545"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Let me tell you something straight off. This is a love story, but not like any you've ever heard. The boy and the girl are far from innocent. Dear lives are lost. And good doesn't win. In some places, there is something ultimately good about endings. In Neverland, that is not the case.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><b>My body is not enough to contain the largeness of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7514925.Tiger_Lily' title='Tiger Lily by Jodi Lynn Anderson' rel='nofollow noopener'>Tiger Lily</a>'s beauty.</b><br/>This is a book of fiction, but not like any I've ever read. It was <b>enthralling</b> in its simplicity, and I absorbed every sound, ever</span>
  <span id="freeText9270968925727650545" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Let me tell you something straight off. This is a love story, but not like any you've ever heard. The boy and the girl are far from innocent. Dear lives are lost. And good doesn't win. In some places, there is something ultimately good about endings. In Neverland, that is not the case.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><b>My body is not enough to contain the largeness of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7514925.Tiger_Lily" title="Tiger Lily by Jodi Lynn Anderson" rel="nofollow noopener">Tiger Lily</a>'s beauty.</b><br>This is a book of fiction, but not like any I've ever read. It was <b>enthralling</b> in its simplicity, and I absorbed every sound, every rustle of the leaves and boom of the waves crashing on tumultuous shores and splash of the mermaids' tails when they retreated into their domain in the depths of the sea, I inhaled every smell, the mustiness of the swamp and the liquor in the pirates' breath, I hurt my legs while running among fallen branches and I gathered dewdrops with Tinker Bell. And just like her, when <b>tragedies</b> occured, and pieces inside of me where broken and scattered, I could do nothing to stop them, but also I could never look away, caught up in the <b>longing</b> and <b>sadness</b> and weakness of the characters.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Find us.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>An invitation. A dare. A challenge. A promise of adventure. In the faraway island of Neverland, the concept of time is fluid. Magical beasts build their nests in the tropical forests, fairies and mermaids interveve in the lives of humans, native tribes keep up with their traditions and never get old, pirates pillage and plunder and fight their never-ending war with the lost boys. <i>The lost boys.</i> Tiger Lily, the daughter of Tik Tok, the shaman of the Sky Eaters tribe, has heard horrible stories about them. People say she is cursed by the crows, and even though she can't tell whether that's true or merely a superstition, she has the heart of a beast, and a tendency to help lost causes. In one of these missions, she comes across the infamous Peter Pan, and she doesn't know what to make of him. He can be vicious and tender at the same time, distant and aloof and then warm and caring, but never consistent. There's something about Tiger Lily that calls to him, and soon the lost boys adopt her like a second family. But her father needs her. Her tribe needs her. Torn between her wildest desires and her need to keep her promises, haunted by a potential murderer and trying to balance her life, Tiger Lily soons discovers the cost of growing up. Of loving and being loved.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Sometimes I think that maybe we are just stories. Like we may as well just be words on a page, because we're only what we've done and what we are going to do.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>After I finished <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7514925.Tiger_Lily" title="Tiger Lily by Jodi Lynn Anderson" rel="nofollow noopener">Tiger Lily</a>, I was left with a <b>bittersweet melancholy</b> that soaked my bones. I am humbled by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/94868.Jodi_Lynn_Anderson" title="Jodi Lynn Anderson" rel="nofollow noopener">Jodi Lynn Anderson</a>'s talent, she managed to capture the very essence of magic, and eloquently channeled it through Tinker Bell's narration. Such narration was one of the highlights of the book; Tink recounted the events that started off when Tiger Lily decided to save an Englishman like whispering a moving tale with a soft voice. The element of foreboding was strong, her descriptions lush, the dialogues scarce and suprisingly I didn't mind at all, because they were not necessary. By means of gestures and delving into the thoughts of every single character, I could experience enough of their emotions. But at the same time, there was a tiny barrier between them and me, and I am grateful for that because otherwise the heartache would be too powerful to handle.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“To love someone was not what she had expected. It was like falling from somewhere high up and breaking in half, and only one person having the secret to the puzzle of putting her back together.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>The mythology of Neverland was intricately woven into the multiple stories of love and loss Tinker Bell witnessed. Tik Tok, Tiger Lily, Peter, they all broke each other, but I cannot tell who started it and who finished it. It was a vicious circle, where everyone was innocent and guilty, from Captain Hook who caused a pang of sumpathy despite his crimes, and quiet and thoughful Pine Sap to the main dramatis personae, who were beautiful and ugly. I cannot claim that I understood Peter, but I suspect that was the whole point. Even he couldn't understand himself. He was fearless and independent yet he needed someone to look after him and overlook his shortcomings. But Tiger Lily could not do that. She had a strong (and sometimes misguided I dare say) sense of honor, she was fierce, brave, and confused, because she couldn't always process or interprete what her heart demanded. What every heart demands.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I never expected that you could have a broken heart and love with it too, so much that it doesn't seem broken at all.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>In the end, what Tiger Lily, and Peter, and I came to understand, was that <b>there are many different and unique kinds of love</b>, and you experience them only once, each with a certain person. Or a certain story. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/94868.Jodi_Lynn_Anderson" title="Jodi Lynn Anderson" rel="nofollow noopener">Jodi Lynn Anderson</a>'s retelling of Neverland was a marvel, and I will always cherish its <b>wildness</b> and <b>weirdness</b> deeply.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1494676933ra/22738729.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/katerina_papas/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/KaterinaPapas" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/Booknest.eu/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="http://booknest.eu/reviews/8-kat-reviews/497-tigerlily" rel="nofollow noopener">BookNest</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="9270968925727650545" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1069367649" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1069367649" />
    <a title="Chantal " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31668723-chantal"><img alt="Chantal " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464626501p2/31668723.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1069367649?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chantal " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chantal " href="/user/show/31668723-chantal">Chantal </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=favourite-books">favourite-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=listened-on-audio">listened-on-audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=best-reads-of-2015">best-reads-of-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=retellings">retellings</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1069367649" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11917835298578653268">Once in a while you read a book that is different from all the others. It hooks itself into your heart and doesn’t let you go until you turn the last page. And when it is done, you realize that it has left a gaping hole inside of you. <br/><br/>For me, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7514925.Tiger_Lily' title='Tiger Lily by Jodi Lynn Anderson' rel='nofollow noopener'>Tiger Lily</a> was that book. I knew how it would end, thought I was prepared, but somehow I still wasn’t. <br/><br/><b>This novel is beautiful, charming and tragic all at the same time.</b> The story was utterly captivating and the writing style so lovely that I feel like the </span>
  <span id="freeText11917835298578653268" style="display:none">Once in a while you read a book that is different from all the others. It hooks itself into your heart and doesn’t let you go until you turn the last page. And when it is done, you realize that it has left a gaping hole inside of you. <br /><br />For me, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7514925.Tiger_Lily" title="Tiger Lily by Jodi Lynn Anderson" rel="nofollow noopener">Tiger Lily</a> was that book. I knew how it would end, thought I was prepared, but somehow I still wasn’t. <br /><br /><b>This novel is beautiful, charming and tragic all at the same time.</b> The story was utterly captivating and the writing style so lovely that I feel like the best way to make you read it is to just give you a quote.<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Let me tell you something straight off. This is a love story, but not like any you've ever heard. The boy and the girl are far from innocent. Dear lives are lost. And good doesn't win.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />I think I knew I would love this story after reading the above sentence alone. And truly, the novel delivers on its promise. <br /><br /><i>Tiger Lily</i> is a <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34268.Peter_Pan" title="Peter Pan by J.M. Barrie" rel="nofollow noopener">Peter Pan</a> retelling which focuses on Tiger Lily but is narrated by Tinker Bell herself, which really added another dimension to the story. But it’s not like any retelling I’ve read before. <b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/94868.Jodi_Lynn_Anderson" title="Jodi Lynn Anderson" rel="nofollow noopener">Jodi Lynn Anderson</a> doesn’t change the setting or circumstances of the story; instead she gives us something more.</b> It diverges from the original tale by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5255014.J_M__Barrie" title="J.M. Barrie" rel="nofollow noopener">J.M. Barrie</a>, and yet it would still fit into it, if that makes any sense. <b>It’s darker and sadder than I imagined and touches on many serious topics such as the relevance of religion, bullying and what it means to be “different”, as well as domestic abuse, forced marriage and rape. But <i>Jodi Lynn Anderson</i> does this in subtle ways so that you never feel like you’re being lectured.</b> <br /><br />Besides the fact that the writing was beautiful, <b>I also loved the characters and their relationships with one another</b>. They were all very complex and well developed – including the villains – and had a lot of depth to them. Tiger Lily, our protagonist, is both a very strong and very vulnerable character. She is quiet and doesn’t like to show other people how she feels for fear of seeming weak. She isn’t always kind but has her heart in the right place. <br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Still, the longer I was around her, the more I could see the colors of her mind and the recesses of her heart. There was a beast in there. But there was also a girl who was afraid of being a beast, and who wondered if other people had beasts in their hearts too. There was strength, and there was also just the determination to look strong. She guarded herself like a secret.<i><b></b></i></i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />Tiger Lily’s and Tinker Bell’s friendship was wonderful. There was such genuineness and loyalty there. It was beautiful, like everything about this novel.<br /><br />And of course, the romance was beautiful too. And heart-breaking.<br /><br /><b>We may have been told at the beginning of the novel that this is a love story, but this book is so much more than that. It’s a story about finding your place in the world, loss and guilt, friendship and loyalty. And loneliness.</b> There is a lot of loneliness. Overall, there is so much more to it than appeared to me at first. <br /><br />Despite it being a fantastical novel (I hesitate calling it fantasy), the thought I had after finishing it was: “Yes, I guess that’s how life is.” I love it when books can make me feel this way. <br /><br />I don’t want to say anything more because I feel like this is a book you just have to experience for yourself. <b>I can only highly recommend <i>Tiger Lily</i>. Even if it doesn't sound like something you'd usually be interested in, I still suggest you give it a try.</b><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11917835298578653268" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2015309429" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2015309429" />
    <a title="Charlotte May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14002983-charlotte-may"><img alt="Charlotte May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596906925p2/14002983.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2015309429?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Charlotte May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Charlotte May" href="/user/show/14002983-charlotte-may">Charlotte May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/18190280-tiger-lily">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=retelling-fairytale">retelling-fairytale</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=tear-jerker">tear-jerker</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2015309429" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15001904534846591899"><i> "To run and run and never worry - that was what they wanted, and I wanted to go with them." </i><br/><br/>Yes for awesome retellings! This book has been on my TBR for years and I had such high hopes. I got it from the library and once I started it I was immediately swept up in this immersive world.<br/><br/>Told from the perspective of Tinker Bell (I know, not what you'd expect from the title!) she follows Tiger Lily as she grows up in the Sky Eaters tribe. They look after one another, and she is the adopted daughter </span>
  <span id="freeText15001904534846591899" style="display:none"><i> "To run and run and never worry - that was what they wanted, and I wanted to go with them." </i><br /><br />Yes for awesome retellings! This book has been on my TBR for years and I had such high hopes. I got it from the library and once I started it I was immediately swept up in this immersive world.<br /><br />Told from the perspective of Tinker Bell (I know, not what you'd expect from the title!) she follows Tiger Lily as she grows up in the Sky Eaters tribe. They look after one another, and she is the adopted daughter of the Shaman, Tik Tok. The most important rule, keep the peace they've made with the pirates, and stay away from Peter Pan and The Lost Boys.<br /><br />Tiger Lily is wild. She is unkempt and uncouth, running around often faster than the boys. She'd rather be off climbing trees and swimming in the lake than sitting still and sewing. When an arranged marriage is forced upon her, she spends even more time away from home, from her vile husband to be and his awful mother.<br /><br />As we expect, she eventually meets Peter Pan, and their relationship is surprising, but strong. She becomes integrated with the Lost Boys, spending more and more time with them. But as we know, she is betrothed, and she cannot hide forever.<br /><br />We meet Hook and Smee, both are whom are nothing like their Disney counterparts. Smee is pretty twisted, whereas Hook is just a drunk. The Englanders come over on their ships and attempt to alter the ways of Tiger Lily's tribe, in particular, Tik Tok's way of life. Philip and the Englanders in particular pissed me right off!<br /><br />Finally, we meet Wendy; and she is portrayed is a much more negative light than we are used to. Perhaps more negative than necessary I thought - because I've never had a problem with Wendy's character before, but it works with this story line.<br /><br />The ending is also a surprise <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Peter leaves with Wendy, goes to London, and grows old, having children of their own. But he does write to Tiger Lily, explaining that he will always love her in one way.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br /><i> "Maybe all her strangeness, her curse, her always feeling like an outsider. had all existed so she could belong here with Peter." </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="15001904534846591899" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1600010719" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1600010719" />
    <a title="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44137919-mikee-readwithmikee"><img alt="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583262285p2/44137919.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1600010719?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" href="/user/show/44137919-mikee-readwithmikee">Mikee (ReadWithMikee)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062003256" href="/book/show/12924326-tiger-lily">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1600010719" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17552161236373299992"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1475734171i/20757325._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Find me on <a href='http://www.instagram.com/readwithmikee' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> & <a href='http://www.twitter.com/readwithmikee' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a>!<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>❝I could hear the quiet in Tiger Lily’s heart. I had never heard it so soft, so at peace, as I did that evening, as she sat with Peter and watched those horses, and dreamed for a moment that she would never have to lose him, or herself.❞</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Rating: ★ ★ ★ ¾<br/><br/>Tiger Lily was my first Peter Pan retelling and although it wasn't as great as I was hoping it would be, I still enjoyed some parts here and there.<br/><br/>The pacing of the story was a bit on the slow side, and no</span>
  <span id="freeText17552161236373299992" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1475734171i/20757325._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Find me on <a href="http://www.instagram.com/readwithmikee" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> &amp; <a href="http://www.twitter.com/readwithmikee" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a>!<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>❝I could hear the quiet in Tiger Lily’s heart. I had never heard it so soft, so at peace, as I did that evening, as she sat with Peter and watched those horses, and dreamed for a moment that she would never have to lose him, or herself.❞</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>Rating: ★ ★ ★ ¾<br><br>Tiger Lily was my first Peter Pan retelling and although it wasn't as great as I was hoping it would be, I still enjoyed some parts here and there.<br><br>The pacing of the story was a bit on the slow side, and not much was going on with the actual storyline. To be honest, I don't think anything happened at all that's worth mentioning. The story was told through Tinker Bell's POV, which worked in some ways and failed in others. Tink's POV always left me feeling bittersweet but at the same time it also made me feel a little detached from the characters. Tiger Lily, as a character, felt a little flat to me. I expected more since the book was named after her. She was a strong character and a bit of a mystery but I just wasn't feeling her as an individual.<br><br>However, I did love Peter and the lost boys. I loved their friendship and their relationship with Tiger Lily. Peter Pan was swoonworthy as he always is. I wasn't really attached to Peter and Tiger Lily as a couple but their relationship was cute and innocent. Even though I didn't ship them, I was still rooting for Peter and Tiger Lily in the end over Peter and Wendy which actually took me by surprise. I love Wendy Darling in the original story but I found myself despising her in this book. I was left feeling a little bitter that she took Peter and the lost boys away from Tiger Lily. I knew that Tiger Lily and Peter weren't going to have a happy ending but I was still hoping anyways.<br><br>The ending did make me a little teary-eyed but it wasn't as sad as everyone made it out to be. It's definitely bittersweet with a hint of tragic because of what could've been but everyone got their happily ever after. Just not in the way that they were hoping or expecting.<br><br>Tiger Lily turned out to be a different book than I expected. Peter Pan, as an original tale, had a touch of magic and fantasy but we barely get any magic in this book. Peter and the lost boys don't even fly! This book isn't one of the best books out there and it probably won't be the most memorable Peter Pan retelling I'll ever read but it was still enjoyable. It's definitely left me craving more Peter Pan retellings!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17552161236373299992" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText10433171665273712417" style="display:none"><br />I’m unsure if I should berate myself or noisily laugh out loud, but I forgot to pick my lunchbox when leaving the metro… and TIGER LILY was inside it as well as an elegant bookmark that I very much enjoyed looking at. <br /><br />I don’t know if I’ll ever get it back.<br /><br />And I also don’t know if I’ll ever finish this book, but I read half of it and the half that I read was beautiful.   <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1365154211" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1365154211" />
    <a title="Nastassja" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7734134-nastassja"><img alt="Nastassja" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596034018p2/7734134.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1365154211?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nastassja" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nastassja" href="/user/show/7734134-nastassja">Nastassja</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">everyone </span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=best-young-adult">best-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=cover-ecstasy">cover-ecstasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=love-triangle">love-triangle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=intiguing-concept">intiguing-concept</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=romance-centered">romance-centered</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=1st-pov">1st-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=excellent-writing">excellent-writing</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1365154211" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13932484349753702271"><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“Let me tell you something straight off. This is a love story, but not like any you’ve heard. The boy and the girl are far from innocent. Dear lives are lost. And good doesn’t win. In some places, there is something ultimately good about endings. In Neverland, that is not the case.”</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br/>This story turned out to be such a pleasant surprise for me! I must confess I am not a fan of <i>Peter Pan</i>, and all retellings I’ve read never left me with the feeling of satisfaction, on the contrary, I was </span>
  <span id="freeText13932484349753702271" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“Let me tell you something straight off. This is a love story, but not like any you’ve heard. The boy and the girl are far from innocent. Dear lives are lost. And good doesn’t win. In some places, there is something ultimately good about endings. In Neverland, that is not the case.”</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br />This story turned out to be such a pleasant surprise for me! I must confess I am not a fan of <i>Peter Pan</i>, and all retellings I’ve read never left me with the feeling of satisfaction, on the contrary, I was always left with deep disappointment. So you can imagine my reluctance to start <i>Tiger Lily</i>, even though most of my friends who read this story enjoyed it immensely. The other reason I postponed reading it, because I somehow thought this book was going to be teen-ish, maybe? I don’t know why I thought so, maybe because Peter Pan – the boy who never grows older - always associated for me with a child's story, and those retellings I read didn’t help the matter of presenting it under a different angle, but, all in all, I was pretty biased starting Tiger Lily. Color me surprised when <b>I found myself captivated by the story from the first pages.</b> It’s not a secret I am an extremely demanding reader, and a rare book manages to capture my attention so easily. Tiger Lily was one of these few.<br /><br />First and foremost thing that makes this book stand out from different Peter Pan retellings is the narrator. <i>Tinker Bell</i>. <b>What a cute, absolutely adorably sweet goodness this tiny faery is!</b> One of the best and most reliable narrators I’ve ever encountered in a book. Tinker shows us the whole story from her point of view and she can’t talk, she can only feel thoughts and emotions of people around her. Main characters almost never interact with Tinker, and surely they never talk to her. She feels herself unnoticed the whole time, but she, on the contrary, sees everything and matters more than she could've ever imagined. Such deep, introspective view on the world around makes the experience of being in Tinker's head an incredibly fascinating experience.<br /><i>
  <blockquote>“Sometimes I think that maybe we are just stories. Like we may as well just be words on a page, because we're only what we've done and what we are going to do. But then I look at the things I've seen and done, and I become a long scrawly line of something important.”</blockquote>
</i><br /> Such tiny, insignificant, from the first look, creature, turned out to be one of the most feeling and understanding persons. I am immensely happy that finally this adorable fae got a role she always deserved, but somehow was overlooked and undervalued in books and movies. <br /><i>
  <blockquote>“A faerie heart is different from a human heart. Human hearts are elastic. They have room for all sorts of passions, and they can break and heal and love again and again. Faerie hearts are evolutionarily less sophisticated. They are small and hard, like tiny grains of sand. Our hearts are too small to love more than one person in a lifetime.”</blockquote>
</i><br />Tinker Bell is our narrator, and, as I said before, through her eyes we observe other characters, and let me tell you that the main ones and secondary ones – every one of them have a real, well-written personalities in this book. It amazes me still that this short (292 pages), considering the average length of a YA fantasy these days (350 and more pages), fantasy fairy-tale manages to have such a <b>well-rounded characters</b>. I swear, <b>every one of them feels real and important to the story</b>. There’s no minor characters; they all matter, and Tinker Bell misses nothing in describing every personality we have. <b>One of the best character-developments ever!</b><br /><br />So, <i>Tiger Lily and Peter Pan</i>... There’s something sad about knowing that this story will never have a happy ending, that we know these two are not meant to be, because there’s someone third. And it worsens the matter when you don’t hate – can’t hate - the third side. Tiger Lily and Peter Pan are perfect for each other: both brave, independent, stand out from the people in their surroundings, both are lonely. They found love and hope in each other, and it was first and pure love, the kind that might last forever. It might, but it won’t, because <b>this fairy-tale has a real life ending</b>. <br /><i>
  <blockquote>“Every kind of love, it seems, is the only one. It doesn’t happen twice. And I never expected that you could have a broken heart and love with it too, so much that it doesn’t seem broken at all.”</blockquote>
</i><br />I was never a fan of how Peter Pan is described in books or movies; there’s always something too childish about him. He’s too carefree, too much laughing, too much of an image that feels too unrealistic. <b>In Tiger Lily we have the real Peter</b>, the one who has all the confidence in the world, but still feels unsure of himself, the one who’s carefree but burdened with fears. <br /><i>
  <blockquote>“As you may have guessed already, Peter had a soul that was always telling itself lies. When he was frightened, his soul told itself, "I'm not frightened." And when something mattered that he couldn't control, Peter's soul told itself, "it doesn't matter." So while I trained my ears and tired to listen hard to him, I couldn't always make out where he was, or what he felt.</blockquote>
</i><br />Tiger Lily is a character who always had a secondary place in stories or was left behind the curtain. Finally a book where the story belongs to her! She is fierce and loyal and loving, but also she’s intimidating and fearless. She is a worrier, but a worrier with a girl’s heart.<br /><i>
  <blockquote>“The longer I was around her, the more I could see the colors of her mind and the recesses of her heart. There was a beast in there. But there was also a girl who was afraid of being a beast, and who wondered if other people had beasts in their hearts too. There was strength, and there was also just the determination to look strong. She guarded herself like a secret.”</blockquote>
</i><br />Ah, a perfect description! <b>I cannot praise the author enough for writing such a beautiful, poignant book that makes you feel all kinds of sad and happy at the same time; a bittersweet kind of story.</b> <br /><br />Apart from having incredibly well-written characters <b>this story touches a lot of important issues: family, religion, friendship, love, self-awareness.</b> I am not one of the people who demands diversity in every book she reads. I prefer diversity only if it’s a well-done diversity, and Tiger Lily is one of such books. <b>I appreciated how strong and important the voice of the diverse character was in this story</b>, how it mattered - really mattered, and made other people around realize the importance of being yourself. I also liked how religion was handled in this book. We all know a saying: <i>The road to hell is paved with good intentions.</i> This one is 100% hit in this book. No matter how good your intentions are, they might have a dire consequences, and our characters will have to face them. <br /><br />◆ This is not a glamorous-happy-ending kind of story. The whole time the feeling of foreboding never left me, I knew something bad was going to happen. I new it from page 1. But knowing that there’s no happy ending made this story somehow even more endearing and heartfelt. I can say it already holds a special place in my heart. What is here left to say? A lot of things, but this is a kind of story you better feel – not read and feel but <i>feel</i> - because this one is sheer emotions encased in a mind of a beautiful creature Tinker Bell is. <b>One of the best 2017 reads! Highly recommended! </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="13932484349753702271" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2260192446?book_show_action=true">Mar 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea Humphrey" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey">Chelsea Humphrey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062003256" href="/book/show/12924326-tiger-lily">review of another edition</a>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47207032-chelsea-humphrey?shelf=library">library</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2260192446" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6744404423422947013">3.5 STARS. I really wanted to love this as much as the majority out there, and it was wholly entertaining with portions of compulsive narration, but I think my expectations were blown too far up by the hype surrounding this one. Props though, for a book to be this old and still have hype surrounding it-color me impressed! Full review to come. <br/><br/><i>Buddy read with Wren and Mary!</i></span>

<div id="review_1134231552" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1134231552" />
    <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner"><img alt="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532688964p2/31461418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1134231552?book_show_action=true">Dec 17, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=retelling">retelling</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1134231552" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1412388360442555532"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437141825i/15542036._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b><u>Reread 07/17</u> : I really don't know why I did this to myself. Perhaps because it's beautiful? <i>Sigh</i>. So beautiful.</b><br/><br/><i>I've finished <i>Tiger Lily</i> 24 hours ago and spent the day reliving some parts and thinking about it, <b>my heart fluttering and suddenly missing a beat when I let my mind drift into Neverland</b>.</i> <br/><br/><b>Here's is why.</b><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1419011023i/12966785._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The story is told in <b>Tinker Bell's POV</b>. Who's <i>mute</i>. Oh, and who can read your thoughts. <i>I knew fairies were such dangerous creatures</i>. Although some readers find it annoying, the rather d</span>
  <span id="freeText1412388360442555532" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437141825i/15542036._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b><u>Reread 07/17</u> : I really don't know why I did this to myself. Perhaps because it's beautiful? <i>Sigh</i>. So beautiful.</b><br><br><i>I've finished <i>Tiger Lily</i> 24 hours ago and spent the day reliving some parts and thinking about it, <b>my heart fluttering and suddenly missing a beat when I let my mind drift into Neverland</b>.</i> <br><br><b>Here's is why.</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1419011023i/12966785._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The story is told in <b>Tinker Bell's POV</b>. Who's <i>mute</i>. Oh, and who can read your thoughts. <i>I knew fairies were such dangerous creatures</i>. Although some readers find it annoying, the rather descriptive kind of writing was a perfect fit for the story in my opinion : it helps to provide a more magical atmosphere, and before realizing it, we're utterly stuck in Neverland. That's true this book can be classed as <i>slow-paced</i> but you know what? <b>I can't think of <u>any part</u> that could have been removed.</b> <br><br>Everything's dazzling. Nothing's useless.<br><br>Moreover, the choice of Tinker Bell as a narrator brought more <b>tension</b>, as she happens to know things characters don't. After <i>years</i> spent utterly annoyed by her character, I find myself understanding her for the very first time - I must confess that I was afraid the little fairy would have prevented me from loving this book - <b><u>Color me surprised</u> : it was in fact the opposite</b>. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1419009845i/12966603._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Tiger Lily</b> doesn't fit in her village's life yet she's always a part of it. Raised by the shaman, <b>Tik Tok</b>, she always knew she was different and - well, she doesn't care. She doesn't care if she's not as pretty as the other girls, as long as she's allowed to hunt and to live her life. She doesn't care to be engaged to a complete brute as long as her father can keep his head up. She doesn't <i>know</i> how to express her feelings, and more than that, <i>she doesn't know that she <b>had to</b>.</i> She's wondrous. She's brave. She makes mistakes. She's <i>real</i>.<br><br>She's anything like female leads I've ever met. <br><b>She's everything I can admire.</b><br><br>The <b>Lost Boys</b> hold my heart in their hands. I fell for them from the very first time Tiger Lily met them, all both awkward, frightened and reckless. Of course <b>Peter</b>'s charm seduced me - <b>enthralled me</b>. I mean, I could see pretty quickly how he managed to take the central place in this bunch of teenagers. He's full of empathy, selflessness, passionate, blunt - yet sometimes he seems to lose his confidence and <i>what does it stay?</i> <b>An adorable but <i>terrified</i> boy whose need to win endlessly fight with his carefulness.</b> <br><br><b>
  <i>Ahem</i>
</b>. Watch out - I might not be able to prevent myself from swearing in that part. <br>Because the <b>Englanders</b>.<br><i>Fucking asshole <b>colonizers</b>.</i> <br><i>You stupid jackasses</i> who think your way of life is the only one that can be taken into account.<br>Who never even <i>try</i> to understand Neverlanders' customs and traditions. <br>And your God. Oh, let's talk about your God. Sorry but it pissed me off so much to hear all this crap and to see stereotypes and judgment enter the village, threatening the sake of every single inhabitant. Deciding that <i>you</i> are judges of what is <i>right</i> and what <i>isn't</i>.<br><br>I wanted to punch something, and I couldn't help but think about the champions of colonization we used to be before, we Europeans - To see how quickly they could insinuate the doubt in everybody's head, taking control - <b>That was both frightening and maddening</b> to be let in the role of the helpless witness, continually dreading the train wreck. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1419009845i/12966605._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <i>You know what? I was so conceited. Overly-confident. Wrongly proud. Because despite the fact I had tears in my eyes at some point, I wasn't broken. I wasn't. Until the letter. <b>That destroying letter</b>. I was torn apart. I read it. I closed the book. And I <b>sobbed</b>.</i>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><i>I took a huge breath when I closed the book then I felt the need to reopen it almost instantly. I'm pretty sure this striking story will be etched in my mind - <br><br><i>Tiger Lily</i> slowly enchanted me, worming its way into my heart - and will haunt me for a long time.</i> <br><br><b>Until I reread it, I'm afraid.</b><br><br>PS : As you can see, I only added one single quote - because I wanted you'd discover this story completely blind. That's what I did, and it was wonderful. 	<br><br>PS2 : In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/292421743?book_show_action=false&amp;page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">her review</a>, Emily May gave this song as a reminder of <i>Tiger Lily</i> and I can't agree more... <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=7GSyXcqvFXA" rel="nofollow noopener">Peter</a><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>
  <a href="https://meetthebookworld.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487851828i/22057164._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_241362635" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/241362635" />
    <a title="Julianna Helms" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5835325-julianna-helms"><img alt="Julianna Helms" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1372835701p2/5835325.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/241362635?book_show_action=true">Nov 29, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julianna Helms" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julianna Helms" href="/user/show/5835325-julianna-helms">Julianna Helms</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062003256" href="/book/show/12924326-tiger-lily">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">tout le monde</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Julianna by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/4140635-brooke">Brooke</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5835325-julianna-helms?shelf=recent-favorites">recent-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5835325-julianna-helms?shelf=own-arc">own-arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5835325-julianna-helms?shelf=books-that-made-me-niagara-falls">books-that-made-me-niagara-falls</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5835325-julianna-helms?shelf=re-read-status">re-read-status</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5835325-julianna-helms?shelf=favorites-all-time">favorites-all-time</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer241362635" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4291598337492319292">**Thank you, THANK YOU, HarperTeen, for giving me this ARC. <3**<br/><br/><b>Actual, full review:</b> Original is <a href='http://thereviewsnews.blogspot.com/2012/06/beasts-in-our-hearts-tiger-lily-book.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>here on my blog</a>.(Note: due to copy-and-paste, formatting and links have been lost. Except for one of them that I manually linked.)<br/><br/><b>starred review.</b><br/><br/>I devoured this book the way a starved man engulfs food. <br/><br/>Tiger Lily has this addictive quality to it, kind of like a drug. It's beautiful and sad and terrible and heartbreaking; it's merciless and benign and desperate and raw. It's feral: words that spill ou</span>
  <span id="freeText4291598337492319292" style="display:none">**Thank you, THANK YOU, HarperTeen, for giving me this ARC. &lt;3**<br /><br /><b>Actual, full review:</b> Original is <a href="http://thereviewsnews.blogspot.com/2012/06/beasts-in-our-hearts-tiger-lily-book.html" rel="nofollow noopener">here on my blog</a>.(Note: due to copy-and-paste, formatting and links have been lost. Except for one of them that I manually linked.)<br /><br /><b>starred review.</b><br /><br />I devoured this book the way a starved man engulfs food. <br /><br />Tiger Lily has this addictive quality to it, kind of like a drug. It's beautiful and sad and terrible and heartbreaking; it's merciless and benign and desperate and raw. It's feral: words that spill out in this incredibly gripping formation, hidden surprises waiting to spring and shock. I highly doubt I have the right words to describe just how amazing this book was, but I will try. That's all I can guarantee.<br /><br />I'm a restless person. I always have to be doing something, and I often don't do the same thing twice. I'm kind of like Peter Pan. It's why I never read a book again right after I finish it, but immediately upon completing Tiger Lily, I had this irresistible urge to drown myself in Jodi's words again and again: I can't get enough of it. I was crippled by this book; I read in class, in the car, everywhere, and it is so predatory it almost made me cry in class. I don't even know how. Quite honestly, I have a strong suspicion that this is now my favorite book--of ever and ever and ever and ever.<br /><br />The characters--mostly Peter--sliced through me with a canyon's depth.<br /><br />This is the Peter Pan I swoon over so badly it's not even funny. This Peter is broken, but he's trying to mend himself and he doesn't want to be broken, so of course he'll lie--to himself, to others, but... mostly himself. That's what made me just stop: at one point, I just had to set the book down and bury my head somewhere. Probably in a heap of tissues. I fell in love with Peter the way Tiger Lily did, and the moment you get to see him past everything--his exterior, his defenseless self--it's like having someone very, very carefully cut your heart out. It hurts, obviously, but it's also defeating. I think that's what made me love this book so much; I guess I'm just a masochist for being such a sucker of bittersweet love stories. Peter Pan is a bewitching boy; I think <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?NR=1&amp;feature=endscreen&amp;v=LBTdJHkAr5A" rel="nofollow noopener">this song</a> describes my feelings about Peter much better than I can. Of course, now that I've spent so much time on Peter Pan, I've totally neglected Tiger Lily and Tinker Bell, our unexpected narrator who actually turned out to be vital to the plot. I'm sure you're all asleep now, so I'll sum up these two and everyone else in the book in a sentence: the characters in this book are all independent--they are wild, but so in very many different ways--yet at one point or another, the decision was dependence, or nothing at all. It's astounding the choices we all make, to see them reflected in these characters so real they were like people burning through the pages.<br /><br />Keep living through Happily Ever Afters; we can just watch them eventually fade. But Tiger Lily does something else: we don't live through the Happily Ever After. We live through the true stories crackling against its wishful disguise.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4291598337492319292" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1617108047" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1617108047" />
    <a title="Heidi The Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7986781-heidi-the-reader"><img alt="Heidi The Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593309467p2/7986781.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1617108047?book_show_action=true">Apr 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heidi The Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heidi The Reader" href="/user/show/7986781-heidi-the-reader">Heidi The Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7986781-heidi-the-reader?shelf=fantasy-and-sci-fi">fantasy-and-sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7986781-heidi-the-reader?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7986781-heidi-the-reader?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7986781-heidi-the-reader?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7986781-heidi-the-reader?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1617108047" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16383298390901144288">This book is an absolutely magical re-telling of the story of Tiger Lily from <i>Peter Pan</i>. The narrator is the fairy, Tinker Bell.<br/><br/>I've always had a soft place in my heart for J. M.Barrie's masterwork. Who among us hasn't wanted to go to a place where you could remain young forever and never grow up?<br/><br/>Jodi Lynn Anderson writes that "never aging" magic of Neverland quite well: <i>"Englanders had come to Neverland before. ... The Englanders had the aging disease. As time went on they turned gray, and shra</i></span>
  <span id="freeText16383298390901144288" style="display:none">This book is an absolutely magical re-telling of the story of Tiger Lily from <i>Peter Pan</i>. The narrator is the fairy, Tinker Bell.<br /><br />I've always had a soft place in my heart for J. M.Barrie's masterwork. Who among us hasn't wanted to go to a place where you could remain young forever and never grow up?<br /><br />Jodi Lynn Anderson writes that "never aging" magic of Neverland quite well: <i>"Englanders had come to Neverland before. ... The Englanders had the aging disease. As time went on they turned gray, and shrank, and, inexplicably, they died. It wasn't that Neverlanders didn't know anything about death, but not as a slow giving in, and certainly not an inevitability."</i> pg 13 (ebook)<br /><br />Tiger Lily's tribe may age, but how old they appear is contingent on something other than time. It's curious and magical.<br /><br />The lost boys come alive in this book with a wildness and unpredictability that I loved: <i>"There was a joyfulness and- at the same time- a fragility about each of them. They were sloppy and uncared for and wildly alert and full of energy."</i> pg 61, ebook.<br /><br />Despite their untamed natures, they are still children: <i>"Straw beds had been separated haphazardly into different areas of the burrow, as if the boys hadn't counted on wanting to live separately when they'd first built it, and only recently pushed themselves as far apart from each other as possible. Still, on one of the beds there was a worn home-sewn toy in the shape of a rabbit, and lying on a pillow, as if it had just been played with, a model of a ship."</i> pg 61, ebook.<br /><br />Peter is the boy who has emotions but doesn't understand them- perpetually young yet always on the verge of growing up.<br /><br />He's fiercely admired by his lost boys and, eventually, Tiger Lily: <i>"Peter picked at his hangnail again. "Actually, I never get sad. It's a waste of time, don't you think?" Tiger Lily didn't answer. She was impressed by the idea of deciding not to be sad. His words made him seem very strong. Impervious."</i> pg 67, ebook<br /><br />Peter is still Peter in this tale. As far as girls go, he can be charming but also rude and aloof: <i>"I think we could be good friends," he said, falling into step with her. "It's perfect because I wouldn't fall in love with you, like I do with the mermaids. Girls always seem so exotic. But it would be okay with you, because you're more like... you know. Not like a girl."</i> pg 77, ebook.<br /><br />Tinker Bell was a sympathetic character in this book, rather than the spoiled, jealous creature that she is portrayed as in <i>Peter Pan</i>: <i>"A faerie heart is different from a human heart. Human hearts are elastic. They have room for all sorts of passions, and they can break and heal and love again and again. Faerie hearts are evolutionarily less sophisticated.... Our hearts are too small to love more than one person in a lifetime. ... I tried to talk sense into my hard little heart. But it had landed on Peter, a creature two hundred times my size and barely aware of me, and there was no prying it loose."</i> pg 77-78, ebook.<br /><br />Hook is extra creepy and villainous: <i>"Neverland had called to him out of legends. A green place. A wild place. And most of all, a place where he'd never grow old. Most people in London hadn't believed it existed, but some still insisted it did, and Hook had cast his lot with them. To get to the island, he'd begged, stolen, and eventually murdered."</i> pg 89-90, ebook.<br /><br />And so is Mr. Smee. But, I'll let Anderson tell you his story. She does a wonderful job of it.<br /><br />The relationship between Tiger Lily, Peter, and Wendy makes a lot more sense in this story. It is less about any potential failings by the girls. The main source of conflict seems to be Peter's emotional immaturity: <i>"As you may have guessed already, Peter had a soul that was always telling itself lies. When he was frightened, his soul told itself, "I'm not frightened." And when something mattered that he couldn't control, Peter's soul told itself, "It doesn't matter."</i> pg 169, ebook.<br /><br />The ending of this book was totally satisfying as well for all of the characters, even little Tinker Bell. I can't say enough good things about it.<br /><br />It's easy to see why fairy tell retellings are so popular with books like <i>Tiger Lily</i> out there, waiting to be discovered.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16383298390901144288" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
