<div id="review_1135016996" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1135016996" />
    <a title="Elena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19673751-elena"><img alt="Elena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1540301866p2/19673751.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1135016996?book_show_action=true">Dec 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elena" href="/user/show/19673751-elena">Elena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19673751-elena?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1135016996" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2675548598596470187">I CAN'T HANDLE THIS RIGHT NOW<br/><br/>_____________________________<br/><br/><br/><b>''This is a love story, but not like any you've heard.''</b><br/><br/>Yup. Tinker Bell didn't lie at all! <br/>Going into this book I knew that it will be a tragic story. I was prepared. But somehow I still wasn't.<br/><br/>Tiger Lily is a Peter Pan retelling, which focuses on Tiger Lily's and Peter Pan's love story. Also, it is written from Tinker Bell's point of view.<br/>I mean: HOW COOL IS THAT?! <br/><br/>I have to warn you guys, if you haven't read the book and you intend to </span>
  <span id="freeText2675548598596470187" style="display:none">I CAN'T HANDLE THIS RIGHT NOW<br /><br />_____________________________<br /><br /><br /><b>''This is a love story, but not like any you've heard.''</b><br /><br />Yup. Tinker Bell didn't lie at all! <br />Going into this book I knew that it will be a tragic story. I was prepared. But somehow I still wasn't.<br /><br />Tiger Lily is a Peter Pan retelling, which focuses on Tiger Lily's and Peter Pan's love story. Also, it is written from Tinker Bell's point of view.<br />I mean: HOW COOL IS THAT?! <br /><br />I have to warn you guys, if you haven't read the book and you intend to (if you don't intend to than let me tell you: READ IT) , then stop reading, because I have to include spoilers. I'm a freakin' mess and I want to share this. :D Just know that this story is magical, captivating, and so so tragic. <br />I loved it. <br /><br /><b>Bye, people, who haven't read this book, because <br />Spoilers </b><br /><br /><br /><br />Where do I even begin with this? <br /><br />Like I said before, I knew, what the ending will be like, but.... knowing doesn't prevent you from feeling the pain, does it? <br /><br /><b>''After Peter left, she lay down on the mattress in the empty house, and forgot to eat.''</b><br /><br />First of all, I have to say, that I absolutely adored Tiger Lily's and Tinker Bell's friendship. Even though Tinker Bell falls in love with Peter as well, her protective instinct when it comes to Tiger Lily, is out of this world. Everything Tinker Bell does, she does in order to help Tiger Lily. It's phenomenal. I love how Tinker Bell never considered, that Tiger Lily actually knew she was there. So when Tiger Lily rescued Tinker Bell from drowning, it was a turning point in their friendship. In this moment it became clear that their friendship is not one-sided.<br /><br />Tiger Lily is not at all, a typical protagonist. She is quiet, can't show any emotions in order to seem strong. And she IS strong, but at the same time she has this vulnerability to her that makes you want to hug the sh*t out of her. And punch the shit out of Wendy and Peter, for that matter.<br /><br />Don't get me wrong Peter made me fall in love with him just like he did with Tiger Lily, Tinker Bell, and so many others. But even people you love need some dispraise. <br />Wendy on the other hand... Hate her. She was this 'perfect' little girl, but you are even able to SMELL how she manipulated Peter and the Lost Boys!<br /><br />Which brings me to the next thing I loved. <br />The Lost Boys were definitely the funny and heartwarming part of this book. I couldn't help but love them!<br /><br />Besides the characters, that were definitely a big reason for why I loved this book so much, I also need to praise Jody Lynn Anderson's writing. It is captivating, it is in itself tragic. <br /><br />5 out of 5 stars, for sure. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2675548598596470187" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_249481537" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/249481537" />
    <a title="Krys" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2798856-krys"><img alt="Krys" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1329103793p2/2798856.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/249481537?book_show_action=true">Dec 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Krys" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Krys" href="/user/show/2798856-krys">Krys</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062003256" href="/book/show/12924326-tiger-lily">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Blech!</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2798856-krys?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2798856-krys?shelf=third-person-narrative">third-person-narrative</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2798856-krys?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2798856-krys?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2798856-krys?shelf=need-to-finish-did-not-finish">need-to-finish-did-not-finish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2798856-krys?shelf=medium-length-book">medium-length-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2798856-krys?shelf=stand-alone">stand-alone</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2798856-krys?shelf=mermaids-sirens-selkies">mermaids-sirens-selkies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2798856-krys?shelf=fairy-pixie-themed">fairy-pixie-themed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2798856-krys?shelf=arcs-i-no-longer-have">arcs-i-no-longer-have</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer249481537&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer249481537" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11038188506731612126"><br/>Tiger Lily is a much anticipated young adult release coming out by NYT bestselling author Jodi Lynn Anderson. I had not heard of it until a copy showed up in my ARCs from Harpercollins. However, the premise immediately intrigued me - a retelling of Peter Pan focusing on Tiger Lily of the Indian tribe? Yes! And with one fell swoop it was placed in the priority pile. Today finally afforded me the chance and, what's more important, the mood to read it. So I cracked it opened and prepared to be amaz</span>
  <span id="freeText11038188506731612126" style="display:none"><br />Tiger Lily is a much anticipated young adult release coming out by NYT bestselling author Jodi Lynn Anderson. I had not heard of it until a copy showed up in my ARCs from Harpercollins. However, the premise immediately intrigued me - a retelling of Peter Pan focusing on Tiger Lily of the Indian tribe? Yes! And with one fell swoop it was placed in the priority pile. Today finally afforded me the chance and, what's more important, the mood to read it. So I cracked it opened and prepared to be amazed. <br /><br />For the record, I love Peter Pan with a big, giant, throbbing heart of love. It's one of my favourite books from my childhood. It's something I've read a lot, and it has inspired a future book related tattoo (that I will get when I can afford to). I love Peter Pan. He was my first literary boyfriend after all... him and his thimble kisses. <br /><br />This book was a disappointment in so many ways. Frankly, I can't say how I really feel about it without offending some people in the mix... so I'm going to tone it down a bit from my initial angry, swearing, hate-filled rant. I have only ever been so thoroughly offended by two other classic retellings in quite the same way as I am with this book... like, to the point where I slammed the book shut in annoyed frustration and just declared outright that I was done. This is the third one ever to hit my STOP button with such unmitigated force. Wow, this one was so not for me.<br /> <br />* Spoilers ahead for those of you who are looking forward to this.. you may want to stop reading *<br /> <br />I'm going to presume that you all know the plot of Peter Pan, so I'll spare you the recap. This one follows Tiger Lily of the native tribe as she grows up and befriends Pan and the Lost Boys. Where this differs from the original is in the fact that the boys and Pan are not magic in the least, and seem to be growing up on the island of Neverland. The Pirates also appear to be aging. Whether this aging problem is explained elsewhere in the book I couldn't tell you, because I didn't finish the last 150 pages. These details were the first indicators that I would be unhappy with this book. <br /><br />Aging? In Neverland? What?!<br /> <br />So where else did it fail? Well, there's the shoddy narration from Tinkerbell, the non-speaking fairy. The story is told in observances from her, which is fine and good, but she frequently switches POVs from third person (when she is talking about Tiger Lily and other characters) to first person (when she is talking about herself). These switches confused me and I lost sight of who the book was about in these intervals. I would actually forget that Tink was narrating until she suddenly had something occur to herself that distracted me from the story at hand... and then I would mistake her voice for Tiger Lily. It would have been better served if she had stuck to one point of view throughout the entire book because this technique just seemed haphazard and unwieldy.<br /> <br />So, what sealed the deal - the handling of the details from that book to this one... The "turning Peter Pan into a YA romance book" factor... I'm thinking specifically of the kiss. The infamous, beautiful kiss scene that we all know and love from the original story; the kiss that Wendy gives to Peter which he mistakes for a thimble. Well, at one point in the book Peter kisses Tiger Lily... a full, on the mouth, lingering, make-out scene worthy of any YA contemporary ... and that's where I shut the book. I could not in any way disassociate what was happening with what I already know about Pan... sweet and innocent Peter who doesn't know kisses from thimbles and wouldn't be able to execute one if his life depended on it... and here he is snogging Tiger Lily? Wrong, it's just wrong... wrong like in March by Geraldine Brooks where Mr. March cheats ON MARMEE OF ALL PEOPLE... wrong like in Wide Sargasso Sea by Jean Rhys where the psycho-sexual/culture judgmental relationship between the two is what drove Bertha mad... bull. Plain and simple. I didn't buy it in those two books and I'm not buying it now... Turning Peter into a non-magic, hormone driven 15 year old? Wrong. Just wrong.<br /> <br />So, clearly I disconnected. I think that is obvious. Retellings are always fraught with peril but in this case it was SO different than what I was expecting and SO not what I wanted it to be. The tone of the novel was not doing anything for me up until that point so it was very easy to put it down. Perhaps the fault lies in me? Perhaps I expect too much and shouldn't... part of that "favourite book" syndrome. Retellings of certain things have got to be really..damn... good... in order to get away with revisiting certain stories. This, however, did not work. It didn't work as a YA book and it has no place in Peter Pan fandom at all. I can't have this book ruin for me what is otherwise a perfect reading experience.<br /> <br />1 out of 5 stars. The only thing redemptive about this book at all is Tiger Lily's transgendered adoptive father, Tik tok... and that's the only reason it gets a star at all. <br /><br />- review courtesy of <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.bibliopunkkreads.com">www.bibliopunkkreads.com</a></span>

<div id="review_285029707" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/285029707" />
    <a title="Crowinator" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/283407-crowinator"><img alt="Crowinator" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604950964p2/283407.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/285029707?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Crowinator" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Crowinator" href="/user/show/283407-crowinator">Crowinator</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062003256" href="/book/show/12924326-tiger-lily">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/283407-crowinator?shelf=vicarious-smoochies">vicarious-smoochies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/283407-crowinator?shelf=arcs">arcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/283407-crowinator?shelf=booklist-review">booklist-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/283407-crowinator?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/283407-crowinator?shelf=genre-fantasy">genre-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/283407-crowinator?shelf=folklore-myths-legends">folklore-myths-legends</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/283407-crowinator?shelf=2012-reads">2012-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/283407-crowinator?shelf=retellings">retellings</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer285029707" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13918994510738212722">**No spoilers for plot, though I've gone and discussed the tone of the ending, which might be considered a spoiler to some.**<br/><br/>"Let me tell you something straight off. This is a love story, but not like any you've heard. The boy and the girl are far from innocent. Dear lives are lost. And good doesn't win. In some places, there is something ultimately good about endings. In Neverland, that is not the case."<br/><br/>This is the story of the thorny romance between Peter Pan and Tiger Lily, before and after t</span>
  <span id="freeText13918994510738212722" style="display:none">**No spoilers for plot, though I've gone and discussed the tone of the ending, which might be considered a spoiler to some.**<br /><br />"Let me tell you something straight off. This is a love story, but not like any you've heard. The boy and the girl are far from innocent. Dear lives are lost. And good doesn't win. In some places, there is something ultimately good about endings. In Neverland, that is not the case."<br /><br />This is the story of the thorny romance between Peter Pan and Tiger Lily, before and after the arrival of Wendy Darling in Neverland. Even with that opening above, I didn't expect this to be so . . . <i>sad</i>. So infused with loneliness and lost love and tragedy. It's beautifully written, and Anderson's re-working of the Peter Pan legend (including many key moments we should all recognize but are woven in subtly) is unconventional and surprisingly realistic. Tiger Lily is such a captivating, complex character in this version, and so is Peter Pan, Tik Tok (her adoptive father), Hook, and especially Tink, the narrator, who as a mute fairy has developed a empathetic kind of telepathy that allows her to see into others' basic thoughts and feelings (a neat trick that makes for a robust story with multiple perspectives, though centered on Tiger Lily). But I'm left with this melancholy, wistful feeling of regret. I suppose changing, like growing up and growing old, has an inherent sadness to it, especially when told from the POV of those being left behind, and I had forgotten that that concept is at the heart of all Peter Pan stories. <br /><br />Tink says at one point, "Sometimes love means not being able to bear seeing the one you love the way they are, when they're not what you hoped for them." That's sort of how I feel about this book. This isn't a criticism, so much as an observation -- it's a very affecting read, but one that left me with a lingering sadness at how it turned out, even though it was in some respects a perfect ending.<br /><br />And now I've gone and jumped this ahead of some of my other books that needs reviews, just to capture this weird feeling. I may do another, fuller review later when I've taken care of those others.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13918994510738212722" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie Monroe" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe">Natalie Monroe</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer777819087" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18171266358568698868"><b>4.25 stars</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>"Let me tell you something straight off. This is a love story, but not like any you've heard. The boy and the girl are far from innocent."</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><b>This little book is wise beyond its years.</b><br/><br/>I don't mean that it's edgy or tries to smash boxes like postmodern fiction. It is what it is, a retelling of Peter Pan. Namely, the story of Tiger Lily and Neverland before the arrival of Wendy Darling. It's wise because of the themes it weaves through the narrative. From the lovely writing to the critic</span>
  <span id="freeText18171266358568698868" style="display:none"><b>4.25 stars</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Let me tell you something straight off. This is a love story, but not like any you've heard. The boy and the girl are far from innocent."</i>
</blockquote><br><br><b>This little book is wise beyond its years.</b><br><br>I don't mean that it's edgy or tries to smash boxes like postmodern fiction. It is what it is, a retelling of Peter Pan. Namely, the story of Tiger Lily and Neverland before the arrival of Wendy Darling. It's wise because of the themes it weaves through the narrative. From the lovely writing to the criticism of colonialism, from the subversion of sexism to the bittersweet ending, it shines like a gem in the sea of YA fairytale retellings.<br><br>First of all, it <b>adds so much to the original story and characters.</b> Neverland is inhabited by three different tribes and is no stranger to the occasional ship that comes ashore. Captain Hook came to Neverland seeking eternal youth, but grows bitter and vengeful when it doesn't happen. Smee is there, but not as the bumbling Disney character we're familiar. The crocodile is there as well alongside the mystery of the ticking clock in his stomach.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1475913108ra/20781113.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Wendy doesn't come in until the last quarter of the book, but Tink hates her for reasons more than petty jealousy. This version of Tink loves Peter too because he noticed her in a world where fairies are treated like flies. But she's also fiercely loyal to Tiger Lily. <br><br>Since Tiger Lily is <b>told from Tink's POV</b>, we actually don't get much insight into the head of the character is named after. Surprisingly, it works. Tiger Lily is a character very much shrouded in mystery even within her own village. As for Peter, he's charming yet scatterbrained, much like what you'd expect from a teenage Casanova with little notion of adult sexuality. Having the story told from their perspectives would actually take away the aura of deliberate mystery surrounding their characters. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Peter loves to make promises. He has the best intentions of keeping them. It makes it worse, somehow, that he doesn't know how to. He thinks he's a nice boy, that's the worst part."</i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1475913108ra/20781114.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And the ending. God, the ending. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[It broke me into tiny little pieces. Peter and Tiger Lily would have never worked long-term. They're both too jagged around the edges; they need someone stable like Pine Sap and Wendy. I know that and I love the idea of Tiger Lily and Pine Sap, but UGH. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>If you've heard of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15745753.Eleanor___Park" title="Eleanor &amp; Park by Rainbow Rowell" rel="nofollow noopener">Eleanor &amp; Park</a> by Rainbow Rowell, you'll know its key marketing pitch is "a story of first love." This is how I would describe Tiger Lily. The story of first love in all its brutal, beautiful honesty.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_282540250" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/282540250" />
    <a title="Mimi Valentine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6110599-mimi-valentine"><img alt="Mimi Valentine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1314137947p2/6110599.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/282540250?book_show_action=true">Feb 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mimi Valentine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mimi Valentine" href="/user/show/6110599-mimi-valentine">Mimi Valentine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062003256" href="/book/show/12924326-tiger-lily">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=pure-awesomeness">pure-awesomeness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=gorgeous-covers">gorgeous-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer282540250" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12926246555697322250"><blockquote><i>"Let me tell you something straight off. This is a love story, but not like any you've heard. The boy and girl are far from innocent. Dear lives are lost. And good doesn't win. In some places, there is something ultimately good about endings. In Neverland, that is not the case..."</i> -Tinker Bell</blockquote><br/>I grew up loving Disney's version of <b>Peter Pan</b>, wishing I could move to Neverland and never grow old. But this book only makes me love it infinitely MORE! <br/><br/>This book is told, not from Tiger Lily's point of v</span>
  <span id="freeText12926246555697322250" style="display:none"><blockquote><i>"Let me tell you something straight off. This is a love story, but not like any you've heard. The boy and girl are far from innocent. Dear lives are lost. And good doesn't win. In some places, there is something ultimately good about endings. In Neverland, that is not the case..."</i> -Tinker Bell</blockquote><br />I grew up loving Disney's version of <b>Peter Pan</b>, wishing I could move to Neverland and never grow old. But this book only makes me love it infinitely MORE! <br /><br />This book is told, not from Tiger Lily's point of view, but Tinker Bell's which is actually SO brilliant! Not only is the empathic little faerie able to know Tiger Lily's thoughts, but she gets a glimpse into other people's too. We get to share Tinker Bell's admiration for Tiger Lily's undeniable courage. And we also get to know her motives, the reasons for little Tink's actions and jealousy, and suddenly everything makes so much more sense. <br /><br />Going into this book, I didn't care much for Tiger Lily. I knew her as the girl who loved Peter and nothing more. But Jodi Lynn Anderson made me <i>care</i> and <i>ache</i> and want to know <i>more</i> about this crow-feathered girl! By the end, I wanted to cry when it was over. I <i>did</i> cry — so much! As much as I love Wendy, part of me wished she wouldn't show up so Peter and Tiger Lily could get a HEA. But my powers of compulsion can only go so far. :')<br /><br />Behind the scenes, Tiger Lily has a <i>horrible</i> life. She's arranged to marry the awful Giant and everyone is scared of her. That's why she craves those nightly escapades with Peter, who is wonderful and sweet in every way. With him, there's adventure and life and promise. He's so <i>different</i> from the boy I thought I knew — Less innocent? More fierce? — but this side of him is just as beautiful. ♥ <br /><br />My only complaint is that this book starts off slow and carries a similar pace throughout. Until Tiger Lily meets Peter, I was never completely pulled under and even then some parts felt dragged on. But the ending, the beauty, and the heartache makes up for it!<br /><br /><b>Tiger Lily</b> is raw and beautiful and heartbreaking and sad. It took my heart, squeezed it into a tiny little ball, then let it fly. Because if you've seen Peter's story, then you know how Tiger Lily's end — and it doesn't end well. But I promise that her story is well worth the read! <br /><br /><b>BUY or BORROW?:</b> If you want to pledge your love to Peter Pan or are even just a little bit curious about the girl with the crow feather in her hair, then you have to buy this book! :) <br /><br />(Original review at <a href="http://diminutivemimi.blogspot.ca/2012/06/review-tiger-lily.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Mimi Valentine's YA Review Blog</a>) </span>
  <a data-text-id="12926246555697322250" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes"><img alt="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598297811p2/1452829.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1973754050?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" href="/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes">Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=2-star">2-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=year-2018">year-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1973754050" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1462304822034534126"><b>Actual Rating: 2.5 Stars</b><br/><br/>Alright. So I said I was going to review this book. I posted the infamous <b>"RTC."</b> but I am thinking honestly it might be a waste of time to do a full blown review in this case.<br/><br/>I <i>liked</i> this book, but here I am barely a week out & already it's fading from my memory in a big way. <br/><br/>I appreciate what was attempted here. A story about Tiger Lily's history with Peter Pan told through the eyes of Tinker Bell. <br/><br/>It didn't shy away from mixing in <b>darker themes</b> with the Neverland we hav</span>
  <span id="freeText1462304822034534126" style="display:none"><b>Actual Rating: 2.5 Stars</b><br /><br />Alright. So I said I was going to review this book. I posted the infamous <b>"RTC."</b> but I am thinking honestly it might be a waste of time to do a full blown review in this case.<br /><br />I <i>liked</i> this book, but here I am barely a week out &amp; already it's fading from my memory in a big way. <br /><br />I appreciate what was attempted here. A story about Tiger Lily's history with Peter Pan told through the eyes of Tinker Bell. <br /><br />It didn't shy away from mixing in <b>darker themes</b> with the Neverland we have all come to know &amp; love, which is actually much closer to the original story of Peter Pan. <br /><br />But I was more than 75% into the book before I felt myself forming any real commitment to the story. It was just sort of... *shrugs* <br /><br />I get the distinct feeling that this book's simple writing style was meant to come off a lot more whimsical &amp; charming than it actually did for me, but that could very well be because it harkened back to the original tale a bit too much for my liking. <br /><br /><b>Spoiler Alert: I didn't enjoy the original.</b><br /><br />Anyhow, I'm sure many people will like this more than I did. It's not bad by any means but I don't expect to remember it a year from now, or at this rate even a month from now. <br /><br />Buddy Read this with Chelsea &amp; Wren! (who I will tag when I get home!)</span>
  <a data-text-id="1462304822034534126" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_1447501734" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1447501734" />
    <a title="Simona B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b"><img alt="Simona B" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408893128p2/5312173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1447501734?book_show_action=true">Nov 20, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Simona B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Simona B" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b">Simona B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062003263" href="/book/show/16108150-tiger-lily">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=fantastic-lit-and-co">fantastic-lit-and-co</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=in-english">in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=2000">2000</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1447501734" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16940655155415170582"><b>4.5</b> -speaking about half stars, uh, Goodreads?<br/><br/><b>"For three days, she kept on studying the horizon, even speaking to it, as if a ship that had already disappeared could hear her."Choose me."<br/>And Peter did choose."</b><br/><br/>This is the story of a girl with crow feathers in her hair and too greedy a heart to be content with just the shreds of a love that could have been. This is the story of a creature so fierce that someone who loved her exactly as she was said once that he would rather die than see her tamed,</span>
  <span id="freeText16940655155415170582" style="display:none"><b>4.5</b> -speaking about half stars, uh, Goodreads?<br><br><b>"For three days, she kept on studying the horizon, even speaking to it, as if a ship that had already disappeared could hear her."Choose me."<br>And Peter did choose."</b><br><br>This is the story of a girl with crow feathers in her hair and too greedy a heart to be content with just the shreds of a love that could have been. This is the story of a creature so fierce that someone who loved her exactly as she was said once that he would rather die than see her tamed, but also so frail that she couldn't help having her heart broken. But you know what's the most telling thing about her? That, at the end of the day, she found it in herself to love all the same. And not in shreds, not in pieces, but wholly.<br><br>But first things first.<br><br>The story is told by <b>Tinker Bell's point of view</b>. When I first heard of this, before starting the book, I wasn't exactly thrilled, because the little fairy is not, to use an euphemism, one of my favourite characters ever -and here, I think, a brief aside is necessary. <b>Peter Pan's story never really spoke to me</b>. Even the Disney version, I didn't like it. I watched it because Hook and Smee made me laugh and I liked all the pretty colours of Neverland, but I kind of loathed all of the characters, including Peter and Wendy -especially Wendy. I found her vain, dull, uninteresting to the point of being annoying. Tinker Bell was just annoying, and girlish. And Peter, well, just say I was never a big fan of his.<br><br>Afetr this books, my opinions haven't changed but for her, Tinker Bell. In <i>Tiger Lily</i>, she is a sparkling (see the irony? The irony!) narrator, fresh and delicate, honest, and, above all, attentive. The author justifies her presence and her role as narrator in a clever and original way which I utterly adored: as a fairy, Tink can 'read' thoughts, memories and feelings. The story is actually told in first person, but we have also such a detailed insight into the other characters' minds that <b>only a third-person narration could have been so exhaustive</b>. The result is a <b>blend of these two narrative techniques</b> that I can't call but absolutely mind-blowing and captivating.<br><br>I read and reread all those passsages in which Tink describes the emotions of the people who surround her. Through her vision, the attraction between Tiger Lily and Peter is a thread that tie theirs hands, Tiger Lily's heart a little beast now shaking with emotion and then roaring with fierceness. <b>All the feelings we witness acquire in this way a plasticity, a vividness</b> that is the cherry on top of Anderson's beautiful writing style.<br><br><b>Tiger Lily</b>'s character: I think it'd be useless for me to try to put into words how I admired and appreciated her development and characterisation. She's no common heroine. She's unable to pretend. She's thirsty and doesn't know it, and when she does know it she's left without water. She's tough, and she's not. She can live without anyone, but she doesn't want to. She seems so aloof ans she's thought to be cursed. Probably she is. Just another one of the thousand amazing things that could be said about her.<br><br><b>“I'm not myself," she offered, guiltily. She softened around Tik Tok, and when she did she was, for those rare moments, girlish.<br>He smiled. "You can never say that. You're just a piece of yourself right now that you don't like.”</b><br><br>I think I've been clear enough about what I think of Peter and Wendy. <br>Probably, all the reasons why an reader would come to despise <b>Peter</b> at the end of this book can easily be summed up with: he's young. He has lived alone for all of his life and probably longs to know where he came from, how he ended up in that island in the middle of nowhere, and he's not mature or selfless enough to understand how his carelessness can hurt other people. As any teenager grappled with his first love, he thinks he'll never feel something stronger than that. Is he to blame? Yes, because there isn't such a thing as the right to break a heart. No, because the belief that such a thing actually exists is what defines youth in itself.<br><b>Wendy</b>, well, I hated her since before, so don't expect me to be unbiased. She appears in just a few pages, but it's enough for her to prove to be the embodiment of everything I hate about 'girliness' (and I say that as a girl). She praises Peter for everything he does, even the stupidest thing, she flutters him, pampers him, fools him, and he falls for that. I don't know if she pretended or really thought he was that awesome, it's the attitude that I can't stand, both hers and his.<br><br>A special mention for <b>Tik Tok</b>. That of religion, and its link to personal identity, is a theme which is very close to my heart, so I was particularly invested in his personal tragedy. I can't find it in me to exlpain how I felt for him and how much anger the Englanders raised in me.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450972289ra/17493464.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>By way of conclusion, if you unconditionally love Peter Pan, don't read this, because the character that's depicted in here it's none like the one you've learned to love. But if you think you're able to stand that, then do it. Go buy the book, bury yourself under a blanket, and read it.<br>Just -and I say it for your sake- don't forget to keep the tissues close.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16940655155415170582" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="elementListBrownSeparator"></div>



  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1739789649" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1739789649" />
    <a title="Julia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13740686-julia"><img alt="Julia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544009372p2/13740686.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1739789649?book_show_action=true">Aug 26, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julia" href="/user/show/13740686-julia">Julia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13740686-julia?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13740686-julia?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13740686-julia?shelf=read-in-english">read-in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13740686-julia?shelf=standalone">standalone</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13740686-julia?shelf=heartache">heartache</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13740686-julia?shelf=brilliant-writing">brilliant-writing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13740686-julia?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1739789649" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17982298995308628170">The only word that perfectly describes <b>Tiger Lily</b> is a Russian word <i>toska</i>.<br/><blockquote>
  <i>“No single word in English renders all the shades of toska. At its deepest and most painful, it is a sensation of great spiritual anguish, often without any specific cause. At less morbid levels it is a dull ache of the soul, a longing with nothing to long for, a sick pining, a vague restlessness, mental throes, yearning. In particular cases it may be the desire for somebody of something specific, nostalgia, love-sickne</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText17982298995308628170" style="display:none">The only word that perfectly describes <b>Tiger Lily</b> is a Russian word <i>toska</i>.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“No single word in English renders all the shades of toska. At its deepest and most painful, it is a sensation of great spiritual anguish, often without any specific cause. At less morbid levels it is a dull ache of the soul, a longing with nothing to long for, a sick pining, a vague restlessness, mental throes, yearning. In particular cases it may be the desire for somebody of something specific, nostalgia, love-sickness. At the lowest level it grades into ennui, boredom.”<br />- Vladimir Nabokov</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>Tiger Lily</b> wasn't boring. But even in moments of joy it was soaked in melancholy, yearning, anguish — all of them mixed together in the ugly proportion that made my heart ache. The feeling you're left with after finishing the book depends only on your perception of the events, but it somehow left me a little bit depressed with all the sadness that was haunting me while I was reading the book. <br /><blockquote>
  <i>Let me tell you something straight off. This is a love story, but not like any you've heard. The boy and the girl are far from innocent. Dear lives are lost. And good doesn't win. In some places, there is something ultimately good about endings. In Neverland, that is not the case.</i>
</blockquote><br />Tiger Lily is fifteen when she is told to be married to a terrible man by her own tribe. She won't longer be a free bird, she'll be forever trapped in the cage of duties her mother-in-law and her future husband will provide with pleasure. But when Tiger Lily meets Peter — the exact same boy everyone told her was dangerous, a cruel savage — her heart misses a beat. Peter is the opposite of everything she's ever known, but is it the good kind of opposite? Good enough to trust him with her heart? The pirates and Englanders arrive, and Tiger Lily starts to question her beliefs and has to be responsible for the consequences of her choices. So when things start to change, she's caught between two fires: her duty and her heart.<br /><br />I won't be trying to compare <b>Tiger Lily</b> to the original story of Peter Pan. I read the book and I watched a couple of movies and cartoons about his adventures, but that was always that one story that stayed in childhood. There are fairy tales you can imagine yourself being a part of: every now and then we hear stories of modern Cinderellas. But when it comes to Peter Pan — and Neverland in particular — it's frozen in time of our childhood, time when we were children, 'cause in real world people do grow up. But Jodi Lynn Anderson managed to remind me that there is one place for Neverland and it's within our hearts. No matter how young or old you are, there is always place for you there. <b>Tiger Lily</b> isn't the story about never growing up, it's quite the opposite. <br /><br />The choice of the narrator of Tiger Lily's story was a very interesting one, although at some moments it made me feel a little bit distant from the story. Being told mostly from the third-person point of view, it gave readers the opportunity to follow not only Tiger Lily, but also Peter and the pirates. I can't say I enjoyed being in the narrator's head, 'cause the voice was frequently full of jealousy and envy, but it managed to tell not only the events, but also what was happening it the heads of the characters. Sometimes I got the feeling that it was told from Tiger Lily's perspective, but the story wouldn't be anything like it was, if the narrator were different.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“I didn't do it to look nice,” she said.<br />“But you do care.”<br />Tiger Lily studied the tree and decided if she did care, she would now choose not to.</i>
</blockquote><br />The novel easily <i>hook</i>ed me from the very beginning, but I fell in love with it only when Peter appeared, even though I loved Tiger Lily's character on her own, too. She might seem as a fierce creature, but don't let her fool you. The meeting with Peter let me get to know the real her: savage, yet fragile, brave, yet hesitant. Tiger Lily might not know much about what loving someone really means, but isn't it this one natural thing that comes to you as time passes? Anderson managed to show her journey so vividly that I couldn't stay indifferent. People do grow in Neverland — but only to the certain defining moment — and I could see Tiger Lily's growth even from then on. Being a 15 y.o girl, she seemed both young and old. <br /><blockquote>
  <i>And to Tiger Lily he suddenly, inexplicably, seemed older than her, and wiser, and the thought hit her hard that it wasn't fair, because she'd suffered, and there he was, looking like he knew so much more than she ever would.</i>
</blockquote><br />Peter wasn't what I expected him to be. He was the one that brought me joy, the way he and the Lost Boys had no idea how to behave in the presence of a girl, how to talk to her, what to say and when to stay silent. But at the same time he was a very complex character on his own, too. Being the leader, the elder brother to all of the Lost Boys, he had to be mature, to be responsible, but at the same time Peter was insecure, sometimes desperate and impulsive, reckless. He was a very controversial character, he was confused about the world, about himself, Tiger Lily, the boys, and no matter what had to radiate the confidence he hadn't always had.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>She hated his need to always win and he hated her coldness during their arguments. They fought about the exact color of the sky and which path they should take on a hunt. They disagreed passionately about whose fish was the best tasting. They could work up extreme hatred for each other at a moment's notice.</i>
</blockquote><br />Tiger Lily and Peter's relationship wasn't one of a kind. And that's why it felt so relatable, real and raw. It wasn't a love from the very first sight, but it was a slow process of building trust, learning to be patient and trying to see each other for what they were. Their relationship perfectly captured the innocence of first love with all its doubts, pain and new feelings. <br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[And it perfectly captured the first heartbreak as well. When Wendy appeared, I instantly hated her. But were there any reasons? <br /><blockquote><i>Of all the things Tiger Lily had thought she might have to be for Peter—strong, brave; to be big and to keep up—she had never thought that the one thing he wanted most from her was simply to show that she believed in him, always and without fail. For Peter, who feared losing so much, this was a great comfort indeed.</i></blockquote><br />I felt <i>myself</i> being Tiger Lily in this story, so watching Wendy being exactly what Peter always needed was a really painful experience that led to the yearning Tiger Lily felt. There was nothing wrong with Wendy, even though I still don't like her character. Where Tiger Lily was competitive and tried to be a worthy rival, Wendy was around Peter when he needed her, she was just the support and comfort he was longing for all this time. And I can't blame him or her, even though I really want to. You can't tell your heart who to love and what to feel. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Apart from telling the love story, <b>Tiger Lily</b> subtly touched very serious topics that have place in our world, too. <br /><blockquote>
  <i>“It’s not for you to judge someone else,” Phillip said. “Judging isn’t what God created us to do.”<br />“But you judge Tik Tok for wearing dresses,” Tiger Lily said. “You don’t think God created him to dress like a woman.”<br />Phillip looked sad. “We all have roles, Tiger Lily. You are a woman and you have a role. I as a man have a role. We all have to be the best we can be at the roles we have. We can’t decide to switch. I feel sad for Tik Tok’s confusion, but I know he will find his way.”</i>
</blockquote><br />No one in the tribe cared what Tiger Lily's father — Tik Tok — looked like, until the first Englander arrived. But being saved by a girl, Phillip wasn't all that grateful. Instead of accepting the way the tribe lived, he decided not to do as the Romans do, when in Rome, by slowly sharing (and sometimes it felt as obtrusion) his beliefs and creed with the tribe. I really loved how the theme of being who you are no matter what people say and having your own beliefs and principles was executed. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[And also how it ended. While Tiger Lily's world was revolving around her nearing wedding and Peter, she missed the moment when her father made up his mind. And it happens. Sometimes we're so absorbed in our own problems and lives, we miss the defining moments our nearest people have. And even though Tiger Lily blamed herself for what happened, it wasn't her fault. We'd never know if she were able to prevent it by being there for him, but Tik Tok made his decision.<br />And all this Englanders' invasion also showed one part of human nature: how sometimes we dictate our own rules, our traditions and lifestyle to those who don't need it.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />The book is mostly character-driven and is focused more on character development, not action. Unlike in the original story, the pirates weren't the central element of <b>Tiger Lily</b>, but it still showed them from the interesting point of view. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The Hook was nothing like I expected him to be: instead he was a broken creature himself, even while holding the whole team in fear. I expected to see more of them, to be honest: Hook and Smee had their scenes, but they were too short and ended too fast. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I'd love to read more about them. I also loved reading about Tiger Lily's friend Pine Sap that was always there for her and her brave friend Moon Eye.<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<blockquote><i>Now there are days when she is content, and days when she’s restless. But there is never a day when she doesn’t see Peter everywhere. Things hurt, and don’t hurt, and hurt again. Eighty years later, and she can still feel surprised that he’s gone. And then so much of the time, she’s glad. But just as she looks for Tik Tok in everything around her, she looks for Peter in the woods, out gathering, in the lagoon, in the burrow that is now abandoned. She goes up on the cliffs from time to time and stands there for hours, continuing her long good-bye. It’s not for lack of loyalty to her husband. It is just that she was fifteen once for the first time, and Peter walked across her heart, and left his footprints there.</i></blockquote><br />And even though the ending they got was probably the best one possible, I still feel this dull ache. For the girl that went through horrible things and became a married medicine woman, and for the girl that gave her heart to the boy who took it and went away. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />This is a love story, but not like any you've heard. Within a really small amount of pages <b>Tiger Lily</b> manages to cause a storm of emotions: from joy to <i>toska</i>. It's the brilliantly written novel that everyone has to experience on their own. It is a love story, but it's also a story of devotion, choices and the hearts that can't be tamed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17982298995308628170" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <i><br/>“Still, the longer I was around her, the more I could see the colors of her mind and the recesses of her heart. There was a beast in there. But there was also a girl who was afraid of being a beast, and who wondered if other people had beasts in their hearts too. There was strength, and there was </i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText16379629478683394842" style="display:none">✪✪✪✪<br /><b>Can retellings of classics be considered classics? BECAUSE THIS NEEDS TO BE. I would love to read this in English class, write argumentative and analytical essays about it, gosh I am such a nerd.</b><br /><blockquote>
  <i><br />“Still, the longer I was around her, the more I could see the colors of her mind and the recesses of her heart. There was a beast in there. But there was also a girl who was afraid of being a beast, and who wondered if other people had beasts in their hearts too. There was strength, and there was also just the determination to look strong. She guarded herself like a secret.” </i>
</blockquote><br />💭<b>Pre-reading thoughts</b>: <br />You say PETER PAN, I say WANT IT.</span>

<div id="review_365461948" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/365461948" />
    <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club"><img alt="Stacia (the 2010 club)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417661051p2/4013351.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/365461948?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacia (the 2010 club)" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club">Stacia (the 2010 club)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=general-fantasy-and-mythology">general-fantasy-and-mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=fairytale-or-classic-retelling">fairytale-or-classic-retelling</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer365461948" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16380882981671017959"><b>Before. This is the before. Before the infamous Wendy, there was Tiger Lily. This is her story.</b><br/><br/>3.5 stars. <i>Expect the unexpected.</i> This is not <i>Peter Pan</i> as you know it. This is Tiger Lily as seen through the eyes of Tinker Bell. <br/><br/>At first, I wasn't sure what to make of a story being told about one person while using the voice of another person (okay, little flying pixie bug thingamajig). It took me several chapters to warm up to the style of writing. I couldn't get past the fact that Tink was flyin</span>
  <span id="freeText16380882981671017959" style="display:none"><b>Before. This is the before. Before the infamous Wendy, there was Tiger Lily. This is her story.</b><br /><br />3.5 stars. <i>Expect the unexpected.</i> This is not <i>Peter Pan</i> as you know it. This is Tiger Lily as seen through the eyes of Tinker Bell. <br /><br />At first, I wasn't sure what to make of a story being told about one person while using the voice of another person (okay, little flying pixie bug thingamajig). It took me several chapters to warm up to the style of writing. I couldn't get past the fact that Tink was flying around and following Tiger Lily, simply describing the daily events as they unfolded. <br /><br /><b>The writing style was intricate, if a bit too contemplative.</b> Fans of books such as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6068551.Shiver__The_Wolves_of_Mercy_Falls___1_" title="Shiver (The Wolves of Mercy Falls, #1) by Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">Shiver</a> will appreciate the concept of <i>Tiger Lily</i>. Subtlety through world and character description is the strength of writing here. If you're looking for a swashbuckling romp, this book might not work for you. This story moves forward in a subtle wave, picking up details of the surroundings as it progresses. Charming phrases and insightful observations make for an almost lulling read at times, even when things become dark.<br /><br /><b>Adventure book this is not.</b> While quiet and informative - often detailed and poetic - there was definitely nothing that would conjure up crazy mental images of pixie dust and nighttime flights. I do admit that I found myself wondering and waiting for the adventures of the Lost Boys and Hook's crew, which never really came into play the way I'd hoped.<br /><br /><b>If you understand this, you'll appreciate the book more.</b> For some reason, my only picture of Tiger Lily is of a cartoon version with a scowl on her face. In this retelling, she is still a bit wary on the outside, but seen through Tink's eyes, she also has a lot of grit and heart. <br /><br /><b>My favorite characters were flipped on me.</b> I have NEVER liked Tink in any version of Peter Pan that I've come across. She was so endearing in this book. I managed to fall in love with Tink and hate Wendy (I hope my friend Wendy Darling does not see this, it's nothing personal!). Oh man, I wanted to rip prissy little Wendy's curls right out of her head. I wanted to scream at Peter for being so enamored of her. <br /><br />Tink's love for both Peter and Tiger Lily was heartbreakingly sweet to watch. One tiny little sprite loved and wanted a boy who couldn't love her back, so she did what she could to take care of both him and the girl that he loved.<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>I confess. I flew back to the burrow on secret, nightly visits. I watched Peter and the boys. I nestled behind Peter's ear one night while he slept. I lay on his chest and listened to him breathe. I wanted to be close to him and smell him and hear his heartbeat.<br /><br />I wanted to be there, having my face touched, defeating a heart like Peter's, but the next best thing was seeing it for Tiger Lily.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><b>I don't know how I feel about Peter being shown as a viable "man" conquest.</b> His youthfulness in this tale was almost seen as a sweet aspect, in the way that an adolescent growing into himself is learning how to charm the ladies. For some reason, he came across as far more capable than how I'd pictured Peter in the past. Wendy was more of a mother to the other lost boys than she was to Peter. I guess the point was made that Peter was more of an equal in this book, especially with the direction that the story headed in.<br /><br /><b>Who should read this book?</b> Anyone who appreciates a story where the strength is in the telling, not the showing. I admit that I generally prefer a book which has more "stuff" going on. I get restless, especially when we're several chapters in and nothing has happened other than one person's life being described, down to the every single side character in the village. This isn't normally the style of writing that I prefer. However, I think the journey won me over in the end. The last 25% of the book was beautiful to witness.<br /><br />Would I read it again? Nah. Once was more than enough.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16380882981671017959" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_362647703" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/362647703" />
    <a title="Keertana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7584700-keertana"><img alt="Keertana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438801223p2/7584700.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/362647703?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Keertana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Keertana" href="/user/show/7584700-keertana">Keertana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062003256" href="/book/show/12924326-tiger-lily">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=kick-ass-heroines">kick-ass-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=books-that-linger">books-that-linger</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=teary-eyed-reads">teary-eyed-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=beautiful-prose">beautiful-prose</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer362647703" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8946357701299128324">4.5/5 Stars <br/><br/>If you’ve ever wanted to visit Neverland, all you’d have to do is pick up a copy of <i> Tiger Lily </i> and immerse yourself in the rich world of pirates, natives, faeries, and the lost boys that Anderson has created so vividly. In many ways, reading <i> Tiger Lily </i> is much like being sprinkled with faerie dust yourself – magical, unbelievable, and emotionally touching. I’ll admit that I only picked up this novel because of its beautiful cover – honestly, how do you resist that? – but I found </span>
  <span id="freeText8946357701299128324" style="display:none">4.5/5 Stars <br /><br />If you’ve ever wanted to visit Neverland, all you’d have to do is pick up a copy of <i> Tiger Lily </i> and immerse yourself in the rich world of pirates, natives, faeries, and the lost boys that Anderson has created so vividly. In many ways, reading <i> Tiger Lily </i> is much like being sprinkled with faerie dust yourself – magical, unbelievable, and emotionally touching. I’ll admit that I only picked up this novel because of its beautiful cover – honestly, how do you resist that? – but I found that it was so much more than its synopsis gave it credit for. There have been more than a fair share of mis-marketed novels over the past few years, and although Tiger Lily had the necessary components to thrill most of the blogging community, I originally thought of it as being just another cheesy fairytale love story. I have never been more glad to admit that I was wrong – very much so. <br /><br />Tiger Lily, the adopted daughter of Tik-Tok, the shaman in the Sky Eaters tribe, is one of the loneliest girls in the world. She has had a reputation of being cursed precede her as she has grown up and struggles to fit in with the tribe that shuns her. Furthermore, she is forced to marry Giant, a brute who mistreats her at every opportunity, against her will. Thus, when Tiger Lily stumbles upon Peter Pan and the Lost Boys one fateful day in the forest, she cannot help but be drawn to this boy who seems to be almost as lonely as she is. Yet, as Tiger Lily will soon find out, first love isn’t all romantic and beautiful as it may seem – it is filled with pain, anger, betrayal, loss and, most importantly, dark change.  <br /><br /><i> Tiger Lily </i> is narrated from Tinker Bell’s point of view – a perspective which I found not only added creativity to this original tale, but also shedded a relatively unbiased light on this story. Furthermore, Tink has access to more than simply Tiger Lily’s side of this tale, making it a multi-faceted romance. Her narration is well-paced, entertaining, and emotionally poignant. I never expected a novel about Neverland to be so dark, painfully sad, or heart-wrenching, but it was. In many ways, that only made me love it even more. We are told from the start that this isn’t a happy love story, yet Anderson writes in such a way that we hope against all hope that Tiger Lily and Peter can still be together. I found that their romance was displayed to us in such a way that we saw it evolve into something deeper, but we also saw the cracks in it.<br /><br />That, more than anything else, is why I loved this story so much. If this novel were told from Tiger Lily’s POV, I’m sure we would have gotten an extremely biased interpretation of her relationship with Peter. However, with Tink as the narrator, we are able to see just how imperfect these two are and while we cannot help but love their romance, we are able to analyze and see it falling apart too. In many ways, <i> Tiger Lily </i> is a novel about first love, but it is also a novel about hope for future loves as well. While it explores the maniac, crazy, and often hormonal madness of a first love, it also presents us with a bittersweet lesson of what it means to truly love, live, and move on. I admired Anderson for her realistic ending and although many readers may be saddened by it, I found myself liking it all the more for its truth. <br /><br />Tiger Lily and Peter’s romance aside, I found that I was surprised by the many other themes in this story as well. For one, I found that the villains we are familiar with such as Captain Hook and Smee are truly explored in depth. We are given insight into what makes them the way they are and are able to understand them better for it. Furthermore, this novel revolves around change, not only in Tiger Lily, but within her village as well. It gives us a closer look into how ideals such as Christianity were spread into Native American tribes and enables us to see just how judgmental our world is compared to the more primitive times. In addition, I found the suicide in this novel to be most heart-breaking. I think it was the one aspect of this story that brought tears to my eyes and I thoroughly sympathized with Tiger Lily’s tough situation. I think it was handled very gracefully as well in the story and its impact on Tiger Lily was especially well developed. <br /><br />All in all, I found <i> Tiger Lily </i> to be unexpected. While I was expecting a cute romance, I instead found a deep, provocative, and thoughtful tale. I loved seeing this story from Anderson’s new perspective and it has renewed in me a greater love of the world J.M. Barrie originally created. Moreover, I admired Anderson’s writing skill in displaying each character’s strengths, weaknesses, and changes throughout the ordeals she put them through. I’ve fallen in love with this story – its realistic quality, its morals, and its characters. While its ending may not have been quite what readers may have wanted, it remains true to the world as we know it, proving that life goes on and continues in the most bittersweet of ways.<br /><br />You can read this review and more on my blog, <a href="http://ivybookbindings.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Ivy Book Bindings.</a> </span>
  <a data-text-id="8946357701299128324" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
